  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

\u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eNot sure if it\'s what causing the exception, but LOBStreamControl has a finalize() method that ends up calling LOBFile.close(), so it is               I don\'t have access to a test environment where I can reproduce this problem, unfortunately. \\n\\n The revision that Mike identified, made some queries that previously stored the entire LOB in memory, use temporary files instead. It sounds reasonable that the IOException goes away when the change is backed out, as it previously didn\'t have to do any I\\/O. That revision did however not change how the temporary files were handled, so I\'d expect the exception to be reproducible also with earlier revisions. \\n\\n Here\'s what I would have done to check that, if I could reproduce the failure: \\n\\n \\n\\t move to a revision before   DERBY-5752   \\n \\n\\n\\n \\n\\t remove all ORDER BY clauses from BlobClob4BlobTest (there are five of them, and the test seems to pass without them, at least in my environment) \\n \\n\\n\\n \\n\\t run BlobClob4BlobTest repeatedly to see if it reproduces the problem \\n \\n\\n\\n By removing the ORDER BY clauses, the test should skip materialization even before   DERBY-5752  , and it should exercise the same code path as the unmodified test does after   DERBY-5752  .              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eTo test whether it is a JVM bug with double and\\/or concurrent close, I wrote the attached program CloseRAF.java. It first attempts to close a RandomAccessFile 1000 times in sequence. If that doesn\'t fail it continues trying (repeatedly) to close a RandomAccessFile from two concurrent threads.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI tested it on a Linux machine with Oracle Java 1.5.0_36, and it fails consistently (though it varies how long it takes before failure) with:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003ejava.io.IOException: Bad file descriptor\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\\tat java.io.RandomAccessFile.close0(Native Method)\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\\tat java.io.RandomAccessFile.close(RandomAccessFile.java:532)\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\\tat CloseRAF$1.run(CloseRAF.java:24)\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\\tat java.lang.Thread.run(Thread.java:637)\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI haven\'t seen it fail yet with Java 6 or Java 7 on the same machine.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf this can also be observed with IBM\'s JVM, it supports the theory that the test failure is caused by a JVM bug with concurrent close. It would happen if LOBStreamControl\'s finalize() method and the normal transaction commit logic ended up closing the same RAF at the same time.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSince a finalizer is involved, reproducing it depends on garbage collection happening at the right moment. I guess the trick with removing ORDER BY clauses in the test may have changed the amount of garbage produced, so that garbage collection happened at a different time.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"knutanders\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13625797_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=knutanders\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"knutanders\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Knut Anders Hatlen\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13625797_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'08\\/Apr\\/13 20:53\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2013-04-08T20:53:37+0000\'\u003e08\\/Apr\\/13 20:53\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    To test whether it is a JVM bug with double and\\/or concurrent close, I wrote the attached program CloseRAF.java. It first attempts to close a RandomAccessFile 1000 times in sequence. If that doesn\'t fail it continues trying (repeatedly) to close a RandomAccessFile from two concurrent threads. \\n\\n I tested it on a Linux machine with Oracle Java 1.5.0_36, and it fails consistently (though it varies how long it takes before failure) with: \\n\\n java.io.IOException: Bad file descriptor \\n\\tat java.io.RandomAccessFile.close0(Native Method) \\n\\tat java.io.RandomAccessFile.close(RandomAccessFile.java:532) \\n\\tat CloseRAF$1.run(CloseRAF.java:24) \\n\\tat java.lang.Thread.run(Thread.java:637) \\n\\n I haven\'t seen it fail yet with Java 6 or Java 7 on the same machine. \\n\\n If this can also be observed with IBM\'s JVM, it supports the theory that the test failure is caused by a JVM bug with concurrent close. It would happen if LOBStreamControl\'s finalize() method and the normal transaction commit logic ended up closing the same RAF at the same time. \\n\\n Since a finalizer is involved, reproducing it depends on garbage collection happening at the right moment. I guess the trick with removing ORDER BY clauses in the test may have changed the amount of garbage produced, so that garbage collection happened at a different time. Hatlen\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13626430_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'09\\/Apr\\/13 09:52\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2013-04-09T09:52:25+0000\'\u003e09\\/Apr\\/13 09:52\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI think this problem could be avoided without introducing more synchronization by reordering how the finalizer performs the cleanup. See the attached patch d6092-1a-reorder-cleanup.diff.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe patch makes the finalizer\'s cleanup code remove the LOBFile from the list of open files before attempting to close it. This way, when commit or rollback calls clearLOBMapping(), it won\'t find the file in the list if the finalizer is about to close it, and it won\'t attempt to close it a second time.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eConversely, if clearLOBMapping() is about to close the file when the finalizer is run, the finalizer will have to wait until it\'s done before it can proceed with removing the file from the list (because clearLOBMapping() synchronizes on the list while it iterates over it). Since the patch makes the finalizer wait with closing the file until it\'s removed from the list, it won\'t try to close it until after clearLOBMapping() is done closing it. In this case, the file will still be closed twice, but it won\'t be closed twice concurrently, and the bug is avoided.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eOn Java 6 and newer the patch shouldn\'t be necessary for correctness. However, it makes it slightly less likely that unnecessary work (that is, double closing) is done, and it doesn\'t increase code complexity, so I think it\'s an improvement regardless of the JVM bug it attempts to work around.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI\'m running the full regression test suite on the patch now.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIt would be good if someone who is able to reproduce the problem could check if the patch helps.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"knutanders\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13626430_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=knutanders\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"knutanders\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Knut Anders Hatlen\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13626430_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'09\\/Apr\\/13 09:52\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2013-04-09T09:52:25+0000\'\u003e09\\/Apr\\/13 09:52\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I think this problem could be avoided without introducing more synchronization by reordering how the finalizer performs the cleanup. See the attached patch d6092-1a-reorder-cleanup.diff. \\n\\n The patch makes the finalizer\'s cleanup code remove the LOBFile from the list of open files before attempting to close it. This way, when commit or rollback calls clearLOBMapping(), it won\'t find the file in the list if the finalizer is about to close it, and it won\'t attempt to close it a second time. \\n\\n Conversely, if clearLOBMapping() is about to close the file when the finalizer is run, the finalizer will have to wait until it\'s done before it can proceed with removing the file from the list (because clearLOBMapping() synchronizes on the list while it iterates over it). Since the patch makes the finalizer wait with closing the file until it\'s removed from the list, it won\'t try to close it until after clearLOBMapping() is done closing it. In this case, the file will still be closed twice, but it won\'t be closed twice concurrently, and the bug is avoided. \\n\\n On Java 6 and newer the patch shouldn\'t be necessary for correctness. However, it makes it slightly less likely that unnecessary work (that is, double closing) is done, and it doesn\'t increase code complexity, so I think it\'s an improvement regardless of the JVM bug it attempts to work around. \\n\\n I\'m running the full regression test suite on the patch now. \\n\\n It would be good if someone who is able to reproduce the problem could check if the patch helps.
